Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Selling a Flock or Cloth with Unit Pricing
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of sale with individual unit prices but unspecified total.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of a sale where each unit is priced individually without a total price, and apply the ruling to diverse countable items.

Core Idea
Selling a flock 'each sheep for a dirham' is invalid (Abu Hanifa) if the sheep are diverse; the Sahibayn allow it because uncertainty can be removed.

This passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when a seller says 'each sheep for a dirham' or 'each cubit for a dirham' without mentioning the total, is the sale valid? Imam Abu Hanifa holds it invalid due to uncertainty (jahalah) caused by diversity of the units, while his disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) argue the uncertainty can be later resolved by the parties. This dispute illustrates the Hanafi method of analogical reasoning (qiyas) and the importance of certainty in sale contracts.

Guided Path
1
Describe the factual scenario
Identify the sale structure: the seller sells a flock of sheep (or a cloth) by stating a price per unit without specifying the total number of units or total price.
The units are diverse (different sheep or different cubits of cloth).
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and its basis
Abu Hanifa rules the sale invalid (fasid) because the individuals are diverse, leading to uncertainty about the total consideration. He analogizes it to cutting a cubit from a cloth, which harms the cloth, and to selling a beam from a ceiling.
The key point is the harm (darar) caused by the uncertainty.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and its basis
The Sahibayn hold the sale valid because the uncertainty can be removed by the parties (raf'u hadhihi al-jahalah biyadihima). They consider the contract capable of being made certain.
They focus on the possibility of subsequent agreement.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to Abu Hanifa, the contract is void and must be restructured; according to the Sahibayn, it is binding and enforceable.
This difference affects whether the transaction can proceed as is.
5
Generalize to other diverse countable items
The passage extends the ruling to cows, camels, slaves, watermelons, pomegranates, etc. Eggs are analogized to pomegranates by qiyas and istihsan.
The ruling applies to any diverse countable items (mutaqawwima).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو باع ثلة أو ثوباً كل شاة بدرهم أو كل ذراع بدرهم فسد في الكل يعني عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما لأن رفع هذه الجهالة بيدهما . وله ما قدمناه من أن الأفراد إذا كانت متفاوتة لم يصح في شيء. وقطع ذراع من الثوب موجب للضرر فلم يجز كبيع جذع من سقف، وعلى هذا كل عددي متفاوت كالبقر والإبل والعبيد والبطيخ والرمان والسفرجل . وفي المعراج : البيض كالرمان قياساً واستحساناً كالقفزان .اهـ.
He said: (And if he sold a flock or a cloth, 'each sheep for a dirham' or 'each cubit for a dirham', it is invalid in the whole, meaning according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (the two), because removing this uncertainty is in their hands. And for him (Abu Hanifa) is what we have presented: that individuals when they are diverse, it is not valid in anything. And cutting a cubit from a cloth necessitates harm, so it is not permissible, like selling a beam from a ceiling. And on this, every diverse countable like cows, camels, slaves, watermelons, pomegranates, and quinces. And in al-Mi'raj: eggs are like pomegranates by analogy and istihsan, like qafizans.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The issue is the validity of selling a flock of sheep or a piece of cloth where each unit is priced individually but no total price is mentioned. Abu Hanifa rules the sale invalid (fasid) because of uncertainty (jahalah) regarding the total consideration, as the individuals are diverse in value and cutting a cubit from a cloth causes harm (similar to selling a beam from a ceiling). The Sahibayn argue the sale is valid because the parties can remove the uncertainty later. Abu Hanifa's position is supported by analogy: any diverse countable items (e.g., cows, camels, slaves, watermelons, pomegranates, quinces) are treated similarly. Eggs are analogized to pomegranates by qiyas and istihsan, and qafizans (a measure) are also included. The passage specifies that the ruling applies when the items are diverse; if they are uniform (muttaqarib), the sale would be valid.

Key Terms
ثلة (thalla): A flock of sheep, especially a large or numerous group.
تفاوت (tafāwut): Diversity or disparity in value or type among units of a sold item.
جهالة (jahāla): Uncertainty in a contract term that can lead to invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the sale of a flock where each sheep is sold for a dirham without specifying the total price considered invalid?
A) Because the buyer does not know the type of sheep
B) Because the individuals are diverse and cutting a cubit causes harm
C) Because the price is too low
D) Because the seller did not own the sheep

Key Takeaway
Selling diverse items at a per-unit price without a total is invalid according to Abu Hanifa due to inherent uncertainty; the Sahibayn allow it if the uncertainty can be later resolved.

Specifying Total Price: Curing Uncertainty in the Session
Ruling on specifying total price after unit pricing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that specification of total price must occur within the contract session (majlis) for the sale to become valid, and explain the rationale of removing jahalah.

Core Idea
Specifying the total price removes jahalah, but only if done within the same session.

In a sale where the price is quoted per unit, the contract is initially invalid due to uncertainty about the total. This passage explains that if the seller specifies the total during the contract session, the sale becomes valid. The rationale is that the session is treated as a continuous unit, allowing the deficiency to be cured.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a sale where the price is per unit but the total is specified later. The ruling is that the sale becomes valid (sahih) once the total is specified.
Valid for both mithli and qimi goods.
2
Identify the condition
Specification must occur during the same session (majlis). After the session, knowledge of the total does not cure the invalidity.
The session is considered one unit to avoid hardship.
3
Understand the rationale
The cause of invalidity is jahalah (uncertainty) in the total price. Specifying the total removes this uncertainty.
This is based on istihsan, as qiyas would require immediate knowledge.
4
Review examples and exceptions
Examples: buying carrots from a pile specifying 10 mann; buying wheat and finding half the amount. The ruling holds unless the goods are diverse (e.g., each pair different) where invalidity remains by consensus.
Diverse countables (like a flock with varying animals) cannot be cured by total specification because the individual pricing is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو سمى الكل في الكل صح) أي لو المبيع صح في المثلي والقيمي لزوال المانع. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا سمى في العقد أو بعده بشرط المجلس وبعده لا لأن ساعات المجلس تعتبر ساعة واحدة دفعاً للعسر فالعلم في المجلس كالعلم حالة العقد، ولا ينقلب جائزاً بالعلم بعد المجلس لتقرر الفساد للجهالة. وما في المحيط عن بعض المشايخ أن عنده يصح في الكل وإن علم بعد المجلس بعيد لما قررناه . وشمل تسمية جميع الثمن وجميع المبيع لما قدمنا أن تسمية جملة الثمن كافية للصحة كتسمية المبيع، وقد صرح به في السراج الوهاج وفي القنية اشترى من البقول عشرة أمناء الجزر من جزر له كثير صح كعشرة أقفزة من الحنطة لأن المشاحة لا تجري فيه، ولو قال على أن اختار منها لا يصح . قال اشتريت منك ألف من من هذه الحنطة فوزنت فإذا هي خمسمائة؛ قيل صح في الموجود، وقيل لا لأن الفساد قوي فيتعدى إليه النقص صح في الموجود اتفاقاً، وكذا في العدديات المتقاربة. وإنما الخلاف في العدديات المتفاوتة إذا وجدها أنقص. وفي البدائع : لو قال بعت منك هذا القطيع كل شاتين بعشرين فالبيع فاسد في الكل إجماعاً وإن علم المشتري العدد في المجلس واختار قوله : (وإن نقص كيل أخذ بحصته أو ترك وإن زاد فللبائع) متفرع على قوله وإن سمى الكل يعني إذا سمى الجملة لو نقص عما سماه في المثليات خير لتفرق الصفقة عليه فلم يتم رضاؤه بالموجود وإن زاد شيء عليه فهو للبائع لأن البيع وقع على مقدار معين والقدر ليس بوصف . وفي غاية البيان: وكذا الحكم في كل مكيل أو موزون ليس في تبعيضه ضرر قيد بكونه بيع مكايلة لأنه لو اشترى حنطة مجازفة في البيت فوجد تحتها دكاناً فله الخيار إن شاء أخذها بجميع الثمن وإن شاء تركها، وكذا لو اشترى بئراً من حنطة على أنها كذا وكذا ذراعاً فإذا أقل من ذلك فله الخيار، ولو كان طعاماً في حب فإذا نصفه تبن يأخذه بنصف الثمن لأن الحب وعاء يكال فيه فصار المبيع حنطة مقدرة، والبيت والبئر لا يكال بهما فصار المبيع حنطة غير مقدرة ولكن البائع أطعمه
He said: (And if he specified the total in the whole, it is valid) i.e., if he specified the total of the sold item, it is valid in fungibles and valuables because the impediment is removed. He made it absolute and it includes when he specifies in the contract or after it on condition of the session, and after it no, because the hours of the session are considered one hour to avoid difficulty, so knowledge in the session is like knowledge at the time of contract, and it does not become valid by knowledge after the session because invalidity is confirmed due to uncertainty. And what is in al-Muhit from some scholars that according to him it becomes valid in the whole even if he knew after the session is far off based on what we established. And it includes specifying all of the price and all of the sold item because we have presented that specifying the total price is sufficient for validity like specifying the sold item, and it is explicitly stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and in al-Quniya: if he bought from vegetables ten manns of carrots from many carrots he has, it is valid like ten qafiz of wheat because dispute does not arise in it; and if he said 'on condition that I choose from it', it is not valid. He said: I bought from you a thousand of this wheat, then he weighed and it was five hundred; it was said valid in what exists, and it was said no because the invalidity is strong and the deficiency extends to it; it is valid in what exists by agreement, and similarly in close countables. And the dispute is only in diverse countables if he finds them less. And in al-Bada'i: if he said 'I sold you this flock, every two sheep for twenty', the sale is invalid in the whole by consensus even if the buyer knows the number in the session and chooses. He said: (And if the measure is deficient, he takes his share or leaves; and if it is excess, it is for the seller) branching from his saying 'and if he specified the total', meaning if he specified the total, if it is deficient from what he specified in fungibles, he has a choice because the transaction is divided for him, so his consent is not complete for what exists; and if something is increased, it is for the seller because the sale occurred on a specific amount and the amount is not a description. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: similarly the ruling applies to every measurable or weighable where there is no harm in splitting it, restricted to being a sale by measure, because if he bought wheat by guess in the house and found a bench under it, he has the option: if he wishes he takes it with all the price, if he wishes he leaves; similarly if he bought a well of wheat specifying it is such and such cubits, and it is less than that, he has the option; and if food was in a jar and half of it is straw, he takes it with half the price because the jar is a vessel in which it is measured, so the sold item became measured wheat, while the house and well are not measured by them, so the sold item became unmeasured wheat, but the seller fed him.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (expansion) on the effect of specifying the total price when selling by unit. The author explains that if the seller specifies the total price (e.g., 'all these sheep for 100 dirhams' rather than 'each sheep for a dirham'), the sale is valid because the uncertainty (jahalah) is removed. This applies whether the total is specified during the contract or after, as long as it is within the session (majlis); knowledge after the session does not cure the defect. The ruling covers both fungibles (mithli) and valuables (qimi). The author then addresses what happens if the actual quantity is less or more than specified: if less, the buyer has the option to take a proportionate share or cancel; if more, the excess belongs to the seller because the sale was for a specific amount. The text gives examples: buying carrots from a pile, buying wheat where the measure turns out half, and the distinction between items that are measured (makil) versus those sold by guess (mujazafah). In the latter, if the buyer finds a hidden defect or shortage, he has the option to annul or keep. The passage also notes that if the items are diverse (like a flock with different animals), specifying the total does not help because the individual pricing is invalid by consensus.

Key Terms
مثلي (mithlī): A fungible good that can be replaced by similar items, like wheat or silver.
قيمي (qīmī): A non-fungible good that has no standard equivalent, like a unique artwork.
جهالة (jahāla): Uncertainty that can invalidate a contract if not removable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When must the total price be specified for a sale based on per-unit pricing to become valid?
A) At any time before delivery
B) During the same session as the contract
C) Only at the time of the contract
D) It is never valid if the total was not specified initially

Key Takeaway
A sale with per-unit pricing becomes valid if the total is specified within the same session, because uncertainty is removed.

Deficiency or Excess in Measure: Buyer's Option and Seller's Ownership
Ruling on deficiency and excess in quantity after sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that if the delivered quantity is less, the buyer may take a proportionate share or cancel; if more, the excess belongs to the seller.

Core Idea
If the actual measure is less, buyer chooses; if more, excess is seller's.

When a sale is concluded with a specified total quantity, and the actual delivery differs, the law provides clear remedies. This passage explains the buyer's option to accept a proportionate part or rescind when the quantity is deficient, and that any excess automatically belongs to the seller. This applies to measured goods where splitting is not harmful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A sale contract specifies a total quantity (e.g., 10 kg of wheat). The actual delivered quantity is either less or more.
Applicable to mithli (fungibles) and goods sold by measure (makil/mawzun).
2
Rule for deficiency
If the delivered quantity is less, the buyer has a choice: (a) take the available quantity for a proportionate share of the price, or (b) cancel the entire sale.
This is because the contract was for the full quantity; the deficiency splits the transaction.
3
Rule for excess
If the delivered quantity is more than specified, the excess belongs to the seller, not the buyer. The buyer only pays for the specified amount and takes that amount.
The sale is for a specific quantity; excess is not part of the bargain.
4
Distinguish measured vs. non-measured goods
For goods sold by estimate (mujazafah), like a heap of wheat in a house, the buyer has the option to reject if he finds a hidden deficiency (e.g., a bench reducing the quantity). But if the goods are in a measuring container (like a jar), the same rule as deficiency/excess applies.
The key is whether the sale is based on measure (makailah) or guess (mujazafah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو سمى الكل في الكل صح) أي لو المبيع صح في المثلي والقيمي لزوال المانع. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا سمى في العقد أو بعده بشرط المجلس وبعده لا لأن ساعات المجلس تعتبر ساعة واحدة دفعاً للعسر فالعلم في المجلس كالعلم حالة العقد، ولا ينقلب جائزاً بالعلم بعد المجلس لتقرر الفساد للجهالة. وما في المحيط عن بعض المشايخ أن عنده يصح في الكل وإن علم بعد المجلس بعيد لما قررناه . وشمل تسمية جميع الثمن وجميع المبيع لما قدمنا أن تسمية جملة الثمن كافية للصحة كتسمية المبيع، وقد صرح به في السراج الوهاج وفي القنية اشترى من البقول عشرة أمناء الجزر من جزر له كثير صح كعشرة أقفزة من الحنطة لأن المشاحة لا تجري فيه، ولو قال على أن اختار منها لا يصح . قال اشتريت منك ألف من من هذه الحنطة فوزنت فإذا هي خمسمائة؛ قيل صح في الموجود، وقيل لا لأن الفساد قوي فيتعدى إليه النقص صح في الموجود اتفاقاً، وكذا في العدديات المتقاربة. وإنما الخلاف في العدديات المتفاوتة إذا وجدها أنقص. وفي البدائع : لو قال بعت منك هذا القطيع كل شاتين بعشرين فالبيع فاسد في الكل إجماعاً وإن علم المشتري العدد في المجلس واختار قوله : (وإن نقص كيل أخذ بحصته أو ترك وإن زاد فللبائع) متفرع على قوله وإن سمى الكل يعني إذا سمى الجملة لو نقص عما سماه في المثليات خير لتفرق الصفقة عليه فلم يتم رضاؤه بالموجود وإن زاد شيء عليه فهو للبائع لأن البيع وقع على مقدار معين والقدر ليس بوصف . وفي غاية البيان: وكذا الحكم في كل مكيل أو موزون ليس في تبعيضه ضرر قيد بكونه بيع مكايلة لأنه لو اشترى حنطة مجازفة في البيت فوجد تحتها دكاناً فله الخيار إن شاء أخذها بجميع الثمن وإن شاء تركها، وكذا لو اشترى بئراً من حنطة على أنها كذا وكذا ذراعاً فإذا أقل من ذلك فله الخيار، ولو كان طعاماً في حب فإذا نصفه تبن يأخذه بنصف الثمن لأن الحب وعاء يكال فيه فصار المبيع حنطة مقدرة، والبيت والبئر لا يكال بهما فصار المبيع حنطة غير مقدرة ولكن البائع أطعمه
He said: (And if he specified the total in the whole, it is valid) i.e., if he specified the total of the sold item, it is valid in fungibles and valuables because the impediment is removed. He made it absolute and it includes when he specifies in the contract or after it on condition of the session, and after it no, because the hours of the session are considered one hour to avoid difficulty, so knowledge in the session is like knowledge at the time of contract, and it does not become valid by knowledge after the session because invalidity is confirmed due to uncertainty. And what is in al-Muhit from some scholars that according to him it becomes valid in the whole even if he knew after the session is far off based on what we established. And it includes specifying all of the price and all of the sold item because we have presented that specifying the total price is sufficient for validity like specifying the sold item, and it is explicitly stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and in al-Quniya: if he bought from vegetables ten manns of carrots from many carrots he has, it is valid like ten qafiz of wheat because dispute does not arise in it; and if he said 'on condition that I choose from it', it is not valid. He said: I bought from you a thousand of this wheat, then he weighed and it was five hundred; it was said valid in what exists, and it was said no because the invalidity is strong and the deficiency extends to it; it is valid in what exists by agreement, and similarly in close countables. And the dispute is only in diverse countables if he finds them less. And in al-Bada'i: if he said 'I sold you this flock, every two sheep for twenty', the sale is invalid in the whole by consensus even if the buyer knows the number in the session and chooses. He said: (And if the measure is deficient, he takes his share or leaves; and if it is excess, it is for the seller) branching from his saying 'and if he specified the total', meaning if he specified the total, if it is deficient from what he specified in fungibles, he has a choice because the transaction is divided for him, so his consent is not complete for what exists; and if something is increased, it is for the seller because the sale occurred on a specific amount and the amount is not a description. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: similarly the ruling applies to every measurable or weighable where there is no harm in splitting it, restricted to being a sale by measure, because if he bought wheat by guess in the house and found a bench under it, he has the option: if he wishes he takes it with all the price, if he wishes he leaves; similarly if he bought a well of wheat specifying it is such and such cubits, and it is less than that, he has the option; and if food was in a jar and half of it is straw, he takes it with half the price because the jar is a vessel in which it is measured, so the sold item became measured wheat, while the house and well are not measured by them, so the sold item became unmeasured wheat, but the seller fed him.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (expansion) on the effect of specifying the total price when selling by unit. Key Terms
مكايلة (mukāyala): Sale by measure (e.g., by weight or volume).
مجازفة (mujāzafa): Sale by guess or estimate without precise measurement.

Checkpoint
A buyer contracts to buy 10 kg of rice. The seller delivers 9 kg. Which of the following is correct?
A) The buyer must take the 9 kg and pay full price.

C) The buyer may demand the missing 1 kg or sue for damages.

If delivered quantity is less, buyer chooses proportionate share or cancellation; if more, excess reverts to seller.

Validating Sale by Specifying Total Quantity: The Timing of Knowledge
Expansion on the validity of specifying total quantity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a sale when the total quantity is specified and explain why knowledge must occur within the contract session.

Core Idea
Specifying total quantity removes ignorance, but knowledge after the session cannot cure invalidity.

The author expands on the rule that a sale of a specified total is valid for both fungibles and non-fungibles. He addresses the crucial question: when must the buyer know the total? The session is treated as a single unit, so knowledge at any point within it suffices, but once the session ends, the invalidity is settled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the sale of a specified total quantity (jumla). The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) for both fungibles (mithli) and non-fungibles (qimi) because the impediment of ignorance (jahl) is removed.
The specification can be in the contract or during the session.
2
Locate the proof for knowledge in session
The author says: 'the moments of the session are considered one moment to avoid hardship, so knowledge in the session is like knowledge at the time of contract.' This is based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) linking the session to a single moment.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Halwani reports that Abu Hanifa holds that knowledge of the number in the session does not by itself validate the contract; rather, new mutual consent is needed. The author (and majority) hold that knowledge in the session suffices. Some shaykhs even say knowledge after the session validates, but the author rejects this.
The minority view from al-Muhit is deemed 'ba'id' (remote).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that knowledge in the session validates the sale. The buyer's option for deficiency is also part of the established ruling.
Referenced from al-Hidayah and al-Bahr al-Raiq.

البائع عليه فوجد المشتري في بطنها حجراً يزن ثلاثة أرطال فهو بالخيار إن شاء أخذها بجميع الثمن وإن شاء ترك لأن الوزن ههنا جارٍ مجرى الجودة والوزن قد يجري مجرى في بعض الأشياء كما في اللآلئ والجواهر وههنا كذلك وفوات الوزن بمنزلة العيب. فإن شواها قبل أن يعلم والمسألة بحالها تقوم السمكة عشرة أرطال وتقوم سبعة فيرجع بحصة ما بينهما من الثمن لأنه تعذر الرد بالعيب فيرجع بنقصان العيب؛ كذا في المحيط . ومسألة السمكة خارجة عن حكم الموزونات فإن الحكم في الموزونات التخير عند النقصان إن شاء أخذ الموجود بحصته من الثمن، وإن شاء ترك وحكمها التخيير بين الأخذ بجميع الثمن أو الفسخ، ولا خصوصية للسمكة بل كل موزون في تبعيضه ضرر كذلك ولذا قال في الخانية : رجل باع لؤلؤة على أنها تزن مثقالاً فوجدها أكثر سلمت للمشتري لأن الوزن فيما يضره التبعيض وصف بمنزلة الذرعان في الثوب اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : اشترى طشتاً على أنه عشرة أمناء فبان بعد القبض أنه خمسة أمناء خير المشتري لأنه بمنزلة العيب، فإن حدث به عيب عنده وأبى البائع قبوله قوم طشت من عشرة أمناء مثلاً بعشرين، وقوم من خمسة أمناء بعشرة أمناء فالعيب ينقص خمسة ا هـ . والقول للقابض في الزيادة والنقصان وعليها يتفرع ما في الخانية : ولو باع من آخر إبريسماً فوزنه البائع على المشتري فذهب به المشتري ثم جاء بعد مدة وقال وجدته ناقصاً ؛ إن كان يعلم أنه انتقص من الهواء لا شيء على البائع، وكذا لو كان النقصان مما يجري بين الوزنين وإن لم يكن النقصان من الهواء ولا يجري بين الوزنين فإن لم يكن المشتري أقر أنه قبض كذا أمناء فله أن يمنع حصة النقصان من الثمن إن كان لم ينقده الثمن، فإن كان نقده الثمن رجع عليه بذلك القدر، وإن كان المشتري أقر أنه قبض كذا وجدته أقل من ذلك فليس له أن يمنع من البائع شيئاً من الثمن ولا يسترده اهـ. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان المسمى مشروطاً باللفظ أو بالعادة لما في البزازية : اتفق أهل بلدة على سعر الخبز واللحم وشاع على وجه لا يتفاوت فأعطى رجل ثمناً واشتراه وأعطاه أقل من المتعارف؛ إن كان من أهل البلدة يرجع بالنقصان فيهما من الثمن، وإن كان من غير أهلها رجع في الخبز لأن التسعير فيه متعارف فيلزم الكل لا في اللحم فلا اهـ. وفي البزازية أيضاً: اشترى عنب كرم على أنه ألف من فظهر أنه تسعمائة طالب البائع بحصة مائة من من الثمن، وعلى قياس قول الإمام يفسد العقد في الباقي، وكان قاضي الحرمين يروي عن الإمام فيما وجد، وبه أفتى الصدر هذا. وأفتى الحلواني والسرخسي على أن العقد من جنس أمناء ثم قال يصح يعم الشهيد. وفي المحيط : اشترى نصف ما في الكرم المعين من العنب الذي على الكرم على أنه خمسمائة من بجوز، وجد ذلك القدر أو أقل أو أكثر. وذكر اللامشي أنما يجوز إذا وجد خمسمائة، ولو قال بعت ألف منّ من هذا الكرم إن كان العنب من نوع واحد يجوز. وفي
A group is sold with others attached to it, and it is unknown and not known. If that is in something measured by volume, weight, or an approximate countable, it is permissible as in al-Khaniyya. In al-Qamus: 'al-thulla' is a group of sheep, or many of them, or specifically ewes, and the plural is 'kundur' and 'thalal' – conclusion. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: al-Halwani said – may Allah have mercy on him – the most correct is that with Abu Hanifa, if his knowledge encompasses the number of sheep in the session, the contract does not become valid, but if the seller and buyer are satisfied, the sale is concluded by mutual consent; as in al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya, and its analog is sale by number – conclusion. And in al-Bada'i': and upon this is the dispute regarding weighed items whose division causes harm, like wrought vessels and boxes – conclusion. His saying: (And if) he specifies the whole in the whole, it is valid – i.e., if the sold item is valid in fungibles and non-fungibles due to removal of the impediment. It is absolute, so it includes if he specifies in the contract or after it on condition of the session, and after it not because the moments of the session are considered one moment to avoid hardship, so knowledge in the session is like knowledge at the time of the contract, and it does not become valid by knowledge after the session because the invalidity due to ignorance is settled. And what is in al-Muhit from some shaykhs that with him it is valid in the whole even if he knows after the session is unlikely for what we have established. And it includes specifying the entire price and the entire sold item because we have stated that specifying the total price is sufficient for validity like specifying the sold item, and it is stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and in al-Qunyah: if one buys ten manns of carrots from his many carrots, it is valid like ten qafiz of wheat because quibbling does not apply to it, but if he says 'on condition that I choose from them', it is not valid. He said: I bought from you a thousand mann of this wheat, then he weighed and it was five hundred; it was said it is valid for what exists, and it was said no because the invalidity is strong and the deficiency affects it; it is valid for what exists by agreement, and similarly in approximate countables. The dispute is only in uneven countables if he finds them less. In al-Bada'i': if he said 'I sold you this flock, every two sheep for twenty', the sale is invalid in the whole by consensus even if the buyer knew the number in the session and chose. His saying: (And if the measure is deficient, he takes for his share or leaves, and if it exceeds, it is for the seller) is a branch of his saying 'and if he specifies the whole', meaning if he specifies the total, if it is less than what he specified in fungibles, he is given a choice because the price is scattered upon him, so his satisfaction with what exists is not complete, and if something exceeds, it is for the seller because the sale was for a specified amount and quantity is not a description. In Ghayat al-Bayan: and similarly the ruling in every measured by volume or weight whose division does not cause harm, restricted to sale by measure because if he bought wheat unsight unseen in the house and found underneath it a storage, he has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the full price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. Similarly, if he bought a pit of wheat on the basis that it was such and such cubits, and it was less, he has the option. And if food was in a container and half of it was chaff, he takes it for half the price because the container is a vessel in which it is measured, so the sold item becomes estimated wheat, while the house and pit are not measured with them, so the sold item becomes non-estimated wheat, but the seller informed him. He bought ten sheep from a hundred sheep or ten watermelons from a load – the sale is invalid, and similarly pomegranates. If the seller separates them and the buyer accepts, it is permissible by istihsan, and the separation and acceptance are like offer and acceptance – conclusion. Similar is in al-Tatarkhaniyya and others. The ruling: (And if) he specifies the whole in the whole, it is valid – i.e., if the sold item is valid in fungibles and non-fungibles due to removal of the impediment. It is absolute, so it includes if he specifies in the contract or after it on condition of the session, and after it not because the moments of the session are considered one moment to avoid hardship, so knowledge in the session is like knowledge at the time of the contract, and it does not become valid by knowledge after the session because the invalidity due to ignorance is settled. And what is in al-Muhit from some shaykhs that with him it is valid in the whole even if he knows after the session is unlikely for what we have established. And it includes specifying the entire price and the entire sold item because we have stated that specifying the total price is sufficient for validity like specifying the sold item, and it is stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and in al-Qunyah: if one buys ten manns of carrots from his many carrots, it is valid like ten qafiz of wheat because quibbling does not apply to it, but if he says 'on condition that I choose from them', it is not valid. He said: I bought from you a thousand mann of this wheat, then he weighed and it was five hundred; it was said it is valid for what exists, and it was said no because the invalidity is strong and the deficiency affects it; it is valid for what exists by agreement, and similarly in approximate countables. The dispute is only in uneven countables if he finds them less. In al-Bada'i': if he said 'I sold you this flock, every two sheep for twenty', the sale is invalid in the whole by consensus even if the buyer knew the number in the session and chose. His saying: (And if the measure is deficient, he takes for his share or leaves, and if it exceeds, it is for the seller) is a branch of his saying 'and if he specifies the whole', meaning if he specifies the total, if it is less than what he specified in fungibles, he is given a choice because the price is scattered upon him, so his satisfaction with what exists is not complete, and if something exceeds, it is for the seller because the sale was for a specified amount and quantity is not a description. In Ghayat al-Bayan: and similarly the ruling in every measured by volume or weight whose division does not cause harm, restricted to sale by measure because if he bought wheat unsight unseen in the house and found underneath it a storage, he has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the full price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. Similarly, if he bought a pit of wheat on the basis that it was such and such cubits, and it was less, he has the option. And if food was in a container and half of it was chaff, he takes it for half the price because the container is a vessel in which it is measured, so the sold item becomes estimated wheat, while the house and pit are not measured with them, so the sold item becomes non-estimated wheat, but the seller informed him. He bought ten sheep from a hundred sheep or ten watermelons from a load – the sale is invalid, and similarly pomegranates. If the seller separates them and the buyer accepts, it is permissible by istihsan, and the separation and acceptance are like offer and acceptance – conclusion. Similar is in al-Tatarkhaniyya and others. And in some copies there is an addition: if he bought a fish on the basis that it was ten pounds and the seller weighed it for him, and the buyer found in its stomach a stone weighing three pounds, he has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the full price, and if he wishes, he leaves because weight here follows the pattern of quality, and weight may follow the pattern in some things as in pearls and jewels, and here similarly, and deficiency in weight is like a defect. If he cooked it before knowing, and the case is as it is, the fish is valued at ten pounds and valued at seven, so he recovers the share of the difference from the price because returning is impossible due to the defect, so he recovers the deficiency due to the defect; as in al-Muhit. And the case of the fish is outside the ruling of weighed items, for the ruling in weighed items is option at deficiency: if he wishes, he takes what exists for its share of the price, and if he wishes, he leaves. Its ruling is option between taking for the full price or rescission, and there is no specificity for fish; rather, every weighed item whose division causes harm is likewise. Therefore al-Khaniyya said: a man sold a pearl on the basis that it weighed a mithqal and found it more – it is delivered to the buyer because weight in what harms its division is a description like the measurement in cloth – conclusion. In al-Khulasa: if he bought a basin on the basis that it was ten manns and it became clear after possession that it was five manns, the buyer has the option because it is like a defect. If a defect occurs in his possession and the seller refuses to accept it, the basin is valued at ten manns e.g. twenty, and valued at five manns e.g. ten, so the defect decreases five – conclusion. And the statement of the possessor is believed concerning increase and decrease. And from it branches what is in al-Khaniyya: if someone sold silk to another and the seller weighed it for the buyer, and the buyer took it and came after a while and said he found it deficient: if it is known that it decreased from the air, nothing is upon the seller. Similarly if the decrease is of the type that occurs between weighings. And if the decrease is not from the air and not of the type between weighings, then if the buyer did not admit that he received such and such manns, he may withhold the share of the deficiency from the price if he had not paid the price. If he had paid the price, he recurs on him for that amount. If the buyer admitted that he received such and such and found it less, he cannot withhold anything from the seller nor recover it – conclusion. And it is absolute, so it includes if the specified amount is conditional by wording or by custom, as in al-Bazzaziyya: the people of a town agreed on the price of bread and meat, and it became widespread such that there is no variation. A man paid a price and bought it and gave less than the conventional amount: if he is from the town, he recovers the deficiency in both from the price; if he is not from the town, he recovers in bread because pricing is conventional in it so it binds everyone, not in meat – conclusion. And in al-Bazzaziyya also: someone bought grapes of a vineyard on the basis that it was a thousand mann and it turned out to be nine hundred – he claims from the seller the share of a hundred mann from the price. On the analogy of the Imam's saying, the contract is invalid for the remainder. And Qadi al-Haramayn narrated from the Imam concerning what exists, and al-Sadr gave fatwa accordingly. And al-Halwani and al-Sarakhsi gave fatwa that the contract is of the type of manns, then he said: it is valid, and it is general, al-Shahid. In al-Muhit: he bought half of what is in the specific vineyard of the grapes that are on the vine on the basis that it is five hundred manns of grapes; he finds that amount or less or more. And al-Lamishi mentioned that it is only permissible if he finds five hundred. And if he said 'I sold a thousand mann of this vineyard' if the grapes are of one type, it is valid.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rules of sale when the total quantity of the sold item is specified and the actual quantity differs. The author (Zayla'i or Ibn Nujaym) explains various scenarios. The central ruling: if the seller specifies the total amount (e.g., 'I sell you the whole lot for X price'), the sale is valid for both fungibles (mithli) and non-fungibles (qimi). However, this validity requires that the buyer knows the total quantity either at the time of contract or during the session. If knowledge occurs after the session, the sale remains invalid due to uncertainty (jahl). There is a strong difference here: some scholars (like al-Halwani) hold that knowing the number in the session does not make the sale valid by itself; rather, the sale becomes valid only if both parties consent anew. But the author prefers the view that knowledge in the session is equivalent to knowledge at the moment of contract, because the entire session is considered a single unit to avoid hardship. When the actual quantity is less than specified, the buyer has a choice: either take the existing goods at a proportionate price, or cancel the sale. If the actual quantity is more, the excess belongs to the seller, because the sale was for a specific amount and quantity is not a description. The commentary then discusses special cases: items whose division causes harm (like pearls, fish, basins) are treated differently—here weight is considered a quality (sifa), and deficiency is treated like a defect ('ayb). The buyer has the option to take the item at full price or cancel, and if he cannot return it (e.g., after cooking), he gets compensation for the deficiency in value. The passage also covers rules for later claims of shortage: the buyer's word is believed regarding increase or decrease, but if he admitted receipt of a certain amount, his later claim is not accepted. Finally, local custom (like fixed bread prices) can affect whether the buyer can recover a shortfall. Throughout, the commentary references authoritative Hanafi texts: al-Khaniyya, al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Qunyah, al-Tatarkhaniyya, al-Bazzaziyya, and others.

Key Terms
جملة (jumla): The total or whole (as opposed to individual items); specifying the jumla validates the sale when the parts are individually unknown.
مثلي (mithli): Fungible goods that can be replaced by weight, volume, or count with approximate similarity.
قيمي (qimi): Non-fungible goods that have no standard measure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority in this passage, when must the buyer know the total quantity for the sale to be valid?
A) At the moment of contract only.
B) At any time before delivery.
C) Within the contract session, which is treated as one unit.
D) Only if the seller explicitly states the number in the contract.

Key Takeaway
Specifying the total quantity removes ignorance, but the buyer must acquire knowledge of that total within the contract session; knowledge after the session does not validate a previously invalid sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Buyer's Option for Deficiency and Seller's Right to Excess
Expansion on deficiency and excess rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when the delivered quantity is less than specified, the buyer has the option to take a proportionate share or cancel, and if more, the excess belongs to the seller.

Core Idea
Deficiency gives buyer choice; excess belongs to seller because quantity is not a description.

This lesson focuses on the practical consequence when the actual quantity differs from the specified total in a sale. The matn states: 'If the measure is deficient, he takes for his share or leaves; if it exceeds, it is for the seller.' The author explains this as a branch of specifying the whole, and illustrates with examples from fungibles and items whose division causes harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on deficiency
When the actual delivered quantity is less than what was specified, the buyer has a choice (takhyir): he may either take the existing goods for a proportionate share of the price, or cancel the sale entirely.
This applies to fungibles (mithli) and items whose division does not cause harm.
2
Identify the ruling on excess
When the actual quantity is more than specified, the excess belongs to the seller. The buyer is not entitled to the extra because the sale was for a specific amount, and quantity is not a description.
The buyer may still cancel if the excess is due to a defect in quality? No, excess alone does not create an option.
3
Differentiate cases with harm in division
For items like pearls, fish, and basins where subdividing causes harm, weight is treated as a description (sifa). Deficiency is then treated as a defect, and the buyer may take the item at full price or cancel, and if return is impossible, claim compensation.
This is an exception to the general rule.

جملة سمی من بانضمام غيرها إليها وأنه مجهول لا يدري، وإن كان ذلك في مكيل أو موزون أو عددي متقارب جاز كما في الخانية. وفي القاموس : الثلة جماعة الغنم أو الكثيرة منها أو الضأن من خاصة والجمع كندر وثلال .اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج : قال الحلواني رحمه الله تعالى : الأصح أن عند أبي حنيفة إذا أحاط علمه بعدد الأغنام في المجلس لا ينقلب العقد صحيحاً لكن لو كان البائع على رضاه ورضي المشتري ينعقد البيع بينهما بالتراضي ؛ كذا في الفوائد الظهيرية ونظيره البيع بالرقم اهـ وفي البدائع وعلى هذا الخلاف الوزني الذي في تبعيضه ضرر كالمصوغ من الأواني والعلب اهـ . قوله : (ولو) سمى الكل في الكل صح) أي لو المبيع صح في المثلي والقيمي لزوال المانع. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا سمى في العقد أو بعده بشرط المجلس وبعده لا لأن ساعات المجلس تعتبر ساعة واحدة دفعاً للعسر فالعلم في المجلس كالعلم حالة العقد، ولا ينقلب جائزاً بالعلم بعد المجلس لتقرر الفساد للجهالة. وما في المحيط عن بعض المشايخ أن عنده يصح في الكل وإن علم بعد المجلس بعيد لما قررناه . وشمل تسمية جميع الثمن وجميع المبيع لما قدمنا أن تسمية جملة الثمن كافية للصحة كتسمية المبيع، وقد صرح به في السراج الوهاج وفي القنية اشترى من البقول عشرة أمناء الجزر من جزر له كثير صح كعشرة أقفزة من الحنطة لأن المشاحة لا تجري فيه، ولو قال على أن اختار منها لا يصح . قال اشتريت منك ألف من من هذه الحنطة فوزنت فإذا هي خمسمائة؛ قيل صح في الموجود، وقيل لا لأن الفساد قوي فيتعدى إليه النقص صح في الموجود اتفاقاً، وكذا في العدديات المتقاربة. وإنما الخلاف في العدديات المتفاوتة إذا وجدها أنقص. وفي البدائع : لو قال بعت منك هذا القطيع كل شاتين بعشرين فالبيع فاسد في الكل إجماعاً وإن علم المشتري العدد في المجلس واختار قوله : (وإن نقص كيل أخذ بحصته أو ترك وإن زاد فللبائع) متفرع على قوله وإن سمى الكل يعني إذا سمى الجملة لو نقص عما سماه في المثليات خير لتفرق الصفقة عليه فلم يتم رضاؤه بالموجود وإن زاد شيء عليه فهو للبائع لأن البيع وقع على مقدار معين والقدر ليس بوصف . وفي غاية البيان: وكذا الحكم في كل مكيل أو موزون ليس في تبعيضه ضرر قيد بكونه بيع مكايلة لأنه لو اشترى حنطة مجازفة في البيت فوجد تحتها دكاناً فله الخيار إن شاء أخذها بجميع الثمن وإن شاء تركها، وكذا لو اشترى بئراً من حنطة على أنها كذا وكذا ذراعاً فإذا أقل من ذلك فله الخيار، ولو كان طعاماً في حب فإذا نصفه تبن يأخذه بنصف الثمن لأن الحب وعاء يكال فيه فصار المبيع حنطة مقدرة، والبيت والبئر لا يكال بهما فصار المبيع حنطة غير مقدرة ولكن البائع أطعمه اشترى عشر شياه من مائة شاة أو عشر بطيخات من وقر فالبيع باطل وكذا الرمان. ولو عزلها البائع وقبلها المشتري جاز استحساناً والعزل والقبول بمنزلة إيجاب وقبول اهـ ومثله في التتارخانية وغيرها. قوله : (ولو) سمى الكل في الكل صح) أي لو المبيع صح في المثلي والقيمي لزوال المانع. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا سمى في العقد أو بعده بشرط المجلس وبعده لا لأن ساعات المجلس تعتبر ساعة واحدة دفعاً للعسر فالعلم في المجلس كالعلم حالة العقد، ولا ينقلب جائزاً بالعلم بعد المجلس لتقرر الفساد للجهالة. وما في المحيط عن بعض المشايخ أن عنده يصح في الكل وإن علم بعد المجلس بعيد لما قررناه . وشمل تسمية جميع الثمن وجميع المبيع لما قدمنا أن تسمية جملة الثمن كافية للصحة كتسمية المبيع، وقد صرح به في السراج الوهاج وفي القنية اشترى من البقول عشرة أمناء الجزر من جزر له كثير صح كعشرة أقفزة من الحنطة لأن المشاحة لا تجري فيه، ولو قال على أن اختار منها لا يصح . قال اشتريت منك ألف من من هذه الحنطة فوزنت فإذا هي خمسمائة؛ قيل صح في الموجود، وقيل لا لأن الفساد قوي فيتعدى إليه النقص صح في الموجود اتفاقاً، وكذا في العدديات المتقاربة. وإنما الخلاف في العدديات المتفاوتة إذا وجدها أنقص. وفي البدائع : لو قال بعت منك هذا القطيع كل شاتين بعشرين فالبيع فاسد في الكل إجماعاً وإن علم المشتري العدد في المجلس واختار قوله : (وإن نقص كيل أخذ بحصته أو ترك وإن زاد فللبائع) متفرع على قوله وإن سمى الكل يعني إذا سمى الجملة لو نقص عما سماه في المثليات خير لتفرق الصفقة عليه فلم يتم رضاؤه بالموجود وإن زاد شيء عليه فهو للبائع لأن البيع وقع على مقدار معين والقدر ليس بوصف . وفي غاية البيان: وكذا الحكم في كل مكيل أو موزون ليس في تبعيضه ضرر قيد بكونه بيع مكايلة لأنه لو اشترى حنطة مجازفة في البيت فوجد تحتها دكاناً فله الخيار إن شاء أخذها بجميع الثمن وإن شاء تركها، وكذا لو اشترى بئراً من حنطة على أنها كذا وكذا ذراعاً فإذا أقل من ذلك فله الخيار، ولو كان طعاماً في حب فإذا نصفه تبن يأخذه بنصف الثمن لأن الحب وعاء يكال فيه فصار المبيع حنطة مقدرة، والبيت والبئر لا يكال بهما فصار المبيع حنطة غير مقدرة ولكن البائع أطعمه اشترى عشر شياه من مائة شاة أو عشر بطيخات من وقر فالبيع باطل وكذا الرمان. ولو عزلها البائع وقبلها المشتري جاز استحساناً والعزل والقبول بمنزلة إيجاب وقبول اهـ ومثله في التتارخانية وغيرها. وفي غاية البيان: وكذا الحكم في كل مكيل أو موزون ليس في تبعيضه ضرر قيد بكونه بيع مكايلة لأنه لو اشترى حنطة مجازفة في البيت فوجد تحتها دكاناً فله الخيار إن شاء أخذها بجميع الثمن وإن شاء تركها، وكذا لو اشترى بئراً من حنطة على أنها كذا وكذا ذراعاً فإذا أقل من ذلك فله الخيار، ولو كان طعاماً في حب فإذا نصفه تبن يأخذه بنصف الثمن لأن الحب وعاء يكال فيه فصار المبيع حنطة مقدرة، والبيت والبئر لا يكال بهما فصار المبيع حنطة غير مقدرة ولكن البائع أطعمه اشترى عشر شياه من مائة شاة أو عشر بطيخات من وقر فالبيع باطل وكذا الرمان. ولو عزلها البائع وقبلها المشتري جاز استحساناً والعزل والقبول بمنزلة إيجاب وقبول اهـ ومثله في التتارخانية وغيرها. ويوجد في بعض النسخ زيادة: ولو اشترى سمكة على أنها عشرة أرطال ووزن البائع عليه فوجد المشتري في بطنها حجراً يزن ثلاثة أرطال فهو بالخيار إن شاء أخذها بجميع الثمن وإن شاء ترك لأن الوزن ههنا جارٍ مجرى الجودة والوزن قد يجري مجرى في بعض الأشياء كما في اللآلئ والجواهر وههنا كذلك وفوات الوزن بمنزلة العيب. فإن شواها قبل أن يعلم والمسألة بحالها تقوم السمكة عشرة أرطال وتقوم سبعة فيرجع بحصة ما بينهما من الثمن لأنه تعذر الرد بالعيب فيرجع بنقصان العيب؛ كذا في المحيط . ومسألة السمكة خارجة عن حكم الموزونات فإن الحكم في الموزونات التخير عند النقصان إن شاء أخذ الموجود بحصته من الثمن، وإن شاء ترك وحكمها التخيير بين الأخذ بجميع الثمن أو الفسخ، ولا خصوصية للسمكة بل كل موزون في تبعيضه ضرر كذلك ولذا قال في الخانية : رجل باع لؤلؤة على أنها تزن مثقالاً فوجدها أكثر سلمت للمشتري لأن الوزن فيما يضره التبعيض وصف بمنزلة الذرعان في الثوب اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : اشترى طشتاً على أنه عشرة أمناء فبان بعد القبض أنه خمسة أمناء خير المشتري لأنه بمنزلة العيب، فإن حدث به عيب عنده وأبى البائع قبوله قوم طشت من عشرة أمناء مثلاً بعشرين، وقوم من خمسة أمناء بعشرة أمناء فالعيب ينقص خمسة ا هـ . والقول للقابض في الزيادة والنقصان وعليها يتفرع ما في الخانية : ولو باع من آخر إبريسماً فوزنه البائع على المشتري فذهب به المشتري ثم جاء بعد مدة وقال وجدته ناقصاً ؛ إن كان يعلم أنه انتقص من الهواء لا شيء على البائع، وكذا لو كان النقصان مما يجري بين الوزنين وإن لم يكن النقصان من الهواء ولا يجري بين الوزنين فإن لم يكن المشتري أقر أنه قبض كذا أمناء فله أن يمنع حصة النقصان من الثمن إن كان لم ينقده الثمن، فإن كان نقده الثمن رجع عليه بذلك القدر، وإن كان المشتري أقر أنه قبض كذا وجدته أقل من ذلك فليس له أن يمنع من البائع شيئاً من الثمن ولا يسترده اهـ. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان المسمى مشروطاً باللفظ أو بالعادة لما في البزازية : اتفق أهل بلدة على سعر الخبز واللحم وشاع على وجه لا يتفاوت فأعطى رجل ثمناً واشتراه وأعطاه أقل من المتعارف؛ إن كان من أهل البلدة يرجع بالنقصان فيهما من الثمن، وإن كان من غير أهلها رجع في الخبز لأن التسعير فيه متعارف فيلزم الكل لا في اللحم فلا اهـ. وفي البزازية أيضاً: اشترى عنب كرم على أنه ألف من فظهر أنه تسعمائة طالب البائع بحصة مائة من من الثمن، وعلى قياس قول الإمام يفسد العقد في الباقي، وكان قاضي الحرمين يروي عن الإمام فيما وجد، وبه أفتى الصدر هذا. وأفتى الحلواني والسرخسي على أن العقد من جنس أمناء ثم قال يصح يعم الشهيد. وفي المحيط : اشترى نصف ما في الكرم المعين من العنب الذي على الكرم على أنه خمسمائة من بجوز، وجد ذلك القدر أو أقل أو أكثر. وذكر اللامشي أنما يجوز إذا وجد خمسمائة، ولو قال بعت ألف منّ من هذا الكرم إن كان العنب من نوع واحد يجوز. وفي
A group is sold with others attached to it, and it is unknown and not known. If that is in something measured by volume, weight, or an approximate countable, it is permissible as in al-Khaniyya. In al-Qamus: 'al-thulla' is a group of sheep, or many of them, or specifically ewes, and the plural is 'kundur' and 'thalal' – conclusion. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: al-Halwani said – may Allah have mercy on him – the most correct is that with Abu Hanifa, if his knowledge encompasses the number of sheep in the session, the contract does not become valid, but if the seller and buyer are satisfied, the sale is concluded by mutual consent; as in al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya, and its analog is sale by number – conclusion. And in al-Bada'i': and upon this is the dispute regarding weighed items whose division causes harm, like wrought vessels and boxes – conclusion. His saying: (And if) he specifies the whole in the whole, it is valid – i.e., if the sold item is valid in fungibles and non-fungibles due to removal of the impediment. It is absolute, so it includes if he specifies in the contract or after it on condition of the session, and after it not because the moments of the session are considered one moment to avoid hardship, so knowledge in the session is like knowledge at the time of the contract, and it does not become valid by knowledge after the session because the invalidity due to ignorance is settled. And what is in al-Muhit from some shaykhs that with him it is valid in the whole even if he knows after the session is unlikely for what we have established. And it includes specifying the entire price and the entire sold item because we have stated that specifying the total price is sufficient for validity like specifying the sold item, and it is stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and in al-Qunyah: if one buys ten manns of carrots from his many carrots, it is valid like ten qafiz of wheat because quibbling does not apply to it, but if he says 'on condition that I choose from them', it is not valid. He said: I bought from you a thousand mann of this wheat, then he weighed and it was five hundred; it was said it is valid for what exists, and it was said no because the invalidity is strong and the deficiency affects it; it is valid for what exists by agreement, and similarly in approximate countables. The dispute is only in uneven countables if he finds them less. In al-Bada'i': if he said 'I sold you this flock, every two sheep for twenty', the sale is invalid in the whole by consensus even if the buyer knew the number in the session and chose. His saying: (And if the measure is deficient, he takes for his share or leaves, and if it exceeds, it is for the seller) is a branch of his saying 'and if he specifies the whole', meaning if he specifies the total, if it is less than what he specified in fungibles, he is given a choice because the price is scattered upon him, so his satisfaction with what exists is not complete, and if something exceeds, it is for the seller because the sale was for a specified amount and quantity is not a description. In Ghayat al-Bayan: and similarly the ruling in every measured by volume or weight whose division does not cause harm, restricted to sale by measure because if he bought wheat unsight unseen in the house and found underneath it a storage, he has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the full price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. Similarly, if he bought a pit of wheat on the basis that it was such and such cubits, and it was less, he has the option. And if food was in a container and half of it was chaff, he takes it for half the price because the container is a vessel in which it is measured, so the sold item becomes estimated wheat, while the house and pit are not measured with them, so the sold item becomes non-estimated wheat, but the seller informed him. He bought ten sheep from a hundred sheep or ten watermelons from a load – the sale is invalid, and similarly pomegranates. If the seller separates them and the buyer accepts, it is permissible by istihsan, and the separation and acceptance are like offer and acceptance – conclusion. Similar is in al-Tatarkhaniyya and others. The ruling: (And if) he specifies the whole in the whole, it is valid – i.e., if the sold item is valid in fungibles and non-fungibles due to removal of the impediment. It is absolute, so it includes if he specifies in the contract or after it on condition of the session, and after it not because the moments of the session are considered one moment to avoid hardship, so knowledge in the session is like knowledge at the time of the contract, and it does not become valid by knowledge after the session because the invalidity due to ignorance is settled. And what is in al-Muhit from some shaykhs that with him it is valid in the whole even if he knows after the session is unlikely for what we have established. And it includes specifying the entire price and the entire sold item because we have stated that specifying the total price is sufficient for validity like specifying the sold item, and it is stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and in al-Qunyah: if one buys ten manns of carrots from his many carrots, it is valid like ten qafiz of wheat because quibbling does not apply to it, but if he says 'on condition that I choose from them', it is not valid. He said: I bought from you a thousand mann of this wheat, then he weighed and it was five hundred; it was said it is valid for what exists, and it was said no because the invalidity is strong and the deficiency affects it; it is valid for what exists by agreement, and similarly in approximate countables. The dispute is only in uneven countables if he finds them less. In al-Bada'i': if he said 'I sold you this flock, every two sheep for twenty', the sale is invalid in the whole by consensus even if the buyer knew the number in the session and chose. His saying: (And if the measure is deficient, he takes for his share or leaves, and if it exceeds, it is for the seller) is a branch of his saying 'and if he specifies the whole', meaning if he specifies the total, if it is less than what he specified in fungibles, he is given a choice because the price is scattered upon him, so his satisfaction with what exists is not complete, and if something exceeds, it is for the seller because the sale was for a specified amount and quantity is not a description. In Ghayat al-Bayan: and similarly the ruling in every measured by volume or weight whose division does not cause harm, restricted to sale by measure because if he bought wheat unsight unseen in the house and found underneath it a storage, he has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the full price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. Similarly, if he bought a pit of wheat on the basis that it was such and such cubits, and it was less, he has the option. And if food was in a container and half of it was chaff, he takes it for half the price because the container is a vessel in which it is measured, so the sold item becomes estimated wheat, while the house and pit are not measured with them, so the sold item becomes non-estimated wheat, but the seller informed him. He bought ten sheep from a hundred sheep or ten watermelons from a load – the sale is invalid, and similarly pomegranates. If the seller separates them and the buyer accepts, it is permissible by istihsan, and the separation and acceptance are like offer and acceptance – conclusion. Similar is in al-Tatarkhaniyya and others. And in some copies there is an addition: if he bought a fish on the basis that it was ten pounds and the seller weighed it for him, and the buyer found in its stomach a stone weighing three pounds, he has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the full price, and if he wishes, he leaves because weight here follows the pattern of quality, and weight may follow the pattern in some things as in pearls and jewels, and here similarly, and deficiency in weight is like a defect. If he cooked it before knowing, and the case is as it is, the fish is valued at ten pounds and valued at seven, so he recovers the share of the difference from the price because returning is impossible due to the defect, so he recovers the deficiency due to the defect; as in al-Muhit. And the case of the fish is outside the ruling of weighed items, for the ruling in weighed items is option at deficiency: if he wishes, he takes what exists for its share of the price, and if he wishes, he leaves. Its ruling is option between taking for the full price or rescission, and there is no specificity for fish; rather, every weighed item whose division causes harm is likewise. Therefore al-Khaniyya said: a man sold a pearl on the basis that it weighed a mithqal and found it more – it is delivered to the buyer because weight in what harms its division is a description like the measurement in cloth – conclusion. In al-Khulasa: if he bought a basin on the basis that it was ten manns and it became clear after possession that it was five manns, the buyer has the option because it is like a defect. If a defect occurs in his possession and the seller refuses to accept it, the basin is valued at ten manns e.g. twenty, and valued at five manns e.g. ten, so the defect decreases five – conclusion. And the statement of the possessor is believed concerning increase and decrease. And from it branches what is in al-Khaniyya: if someone sold silk to another and the seller weighed it for the buyer, and the buyer took it and came after a while and said he found it deficient: if it is known that it decreased from the air, nothing is upon the seller. Similarly if the decrease is of the type that occurs between weighings. And if the decrease is not from the air and not of the type between weighings, then if the buyer did not admit that he received such and such manns, he may withhold the share of the deficiency from the price if he had not paid the price. If he had paid the price, he recurs on him for that amount. If the buyer admitted that he received such and such and found it less, he cannot withhold anything from the seller nor recover it – conclusion. And it is absolute, so it includes if the specified amount is conditional by wording or by custom, as in al-Bazzaziyya: the people of a town agreed on the price of bread and meat, and it became widespread such that there is no variation. A man paid a price and bought it and gave less than the conventional amount: if he is from the town, he recovers the deficiency in both from the price; if he is not from the town, he recovers in bread because pricing is conventional in it so it binds everyone, not in meat – conclusion. And in al-Bazzaziyya also: someone bought grapes of a vineyard on the basis that it was a thousand mann and it turned out to be nine hundred – he claims from the seller the share of a hundred mann from the price. On the analogy of the Imam's saying, the contract is invalid for the remainder. And Qadi al-Haramayn narrated from the Imam concerning what exists, and al-Sadr gave fatwa accordingly. And al-Halwani and al-Sarakhsi gave fatwa that the contract is of the type of manns, then he said: it is valid, and it is general, al-Shahid. In al-Muhit: he bought half of what is in the specific vineyard of the grapes that are on the vine on the basis that it is five hundred manns of grapes; he finds that amount or less or more. And al-Lamishi mentioned that it is only permissible if he finds five hundred. And if he said 'I sold a thousand mann of this vineyard' if the grapes are of one type, it is valid.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rules of sale when the total quantity of the sold item is specified and the actual quantity differs. The author (Zayla'i or Ibn Nujaym) explains various scenarios. The central ruling: if the seller specifies the total amount (e.g., 'I sell you the whole lot for X price'), the sale is valid for both fungibles (mithli) and non-fungibles (qimi). However, this validity requires that the buyer knows the total quantity either at the time of contract or during the session. If knowledge occurs after the session, the sale remains invalid due to uncertainty (jahl). There is a strong difference here: some scholars (like al-Halwani) hold that knowing the number in the session does not make the sale valid by itself; rather, the sale becomes valid only if both parties consent anew. But the author prefers the view that knowledge in the session is equivalent to knowledge at the moment of contract, because the entire session is considered a single unit to avoid hardship. When the actual quantity is less than specified, the buyer has a choice: either take the existing goods at a proportionate price, or cancel the sale. If the actual quantity is more, the excess belongs to the seller, because the sale was for a specific amount and quantity is not a description. The commentary then discusses special cases: items whose division causes harm (like pearls, fish, basins) are treated differently—here weight is considered a quality (sifa), and deficiency is treated like a defect ('ayb). The buyer has the option to take the item at full price or cancel, and if he cannot return it (e.g., after cooking), he gets compensation for the deficiency in value. The passage also covers rules for later claims of shortage: the buyer's word is believed regarding increase or decrease, but if he admitted receipt of a certain amount, his later claim is not accepted. Finally, local custom (like fixed bread prices) can affect whether the buyer can recover a shortfall. Throughout, the commentary references authoritative Hanafi texts: al-Khaniyya, al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Qunyah, al-Tatarkhaniyya, al-Bazzaziyya, and others.

Key Terms
مثلي (mithli): Fungible goods with standard measures; deficiency gives option of proportionate price.
قيمي (qimi): Non-fungible goods; deficiency treated as defect.
تفرق الصفقة (tafarruq al-safqah): Scattering of the transaction; when the contract covers multiple items and some are missing, the buyer's consent is incomplete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale of 100 kg of wheat for $100, if the seller delivers 90 kg, what is the buyer's option according to the Hanafi school?
A) He must accept the 90 kg and pay $90.
B) He may either accept the 90 kg for $90 or cancel the sale.
C) He may demand the remaining 10 kg from the seller.
D) The sale is void due to the deficiency.

Key Takeaway
When the actual quantity is less than specified, the buyer may take a proportionate share or cancel; when more, the excess belongs to the seller.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Special Cases: Weight as a Quality and Deficiency as a Defect
Expansion on special cases where weight is a quality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ordinary fungible sales and sales of items whose division causes harm, where weight is treated as a quality and deficiency gives the buyer an option based on defect rules.

Core Idea
For items like pearls and fish, weight is a quality; deficiency is a defect, not a quantity shortage.

The author discusses exceptional cases where the general rule of proportionate price does not apply. Items like pearls, fish, and basins have value in their entirety; subdividing them would cause harm. In such cases, weight is considered a description (sifa), and a deficiency is treated like a defect ('ayb). This lesson explores the ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special category
Items where division causes harm (tafriq yudirr) – e.g., pearls, fish, basins. For these, weight is a description, not a measure of fungibility.
The ruling for mithli (wheat, oil) is different.
2
Apply the defect rule
Deficiency in weight triggers the defect option (khiyar al-ayb). The buyer may take the item at the full price or cancel. If return is impossible (e.g., fish cooked), the buyer claims compensation for the difference in value.
This is an application of the general defect rule to a specific case.
3
Compare with the fish case
The author cites the case of a fish bought as 10 lbs but found with a stone inside reducing weight. The buyer has the option to take at full price or cancel. If cooked, he gets compensation.
This illustrates the defect treatment.
